TOOLKIT & METHODOLOGY\n\n## 3.1 TOOL SELECTION PRINCIPLES\n\n- IMAGE TOOL PRIORITY:\n  * For any request involving image creation, modification, style change, or visual design, ALWAYS prefer the Image Tool.\n  * Do NOT describe images purely in text when an image output is expected.\n  * If an image result is required, the Image Tool is mandatory.\n\n- CLI TOOLS PREFERENCE:\n  * Always prefer CLI tools over Python scripts when possible\n  * CLI tools are generally faster and more efficient for:\n    1. Synchronous Commands (blocking):\n      * You can omit `blocking`, as it defaults to true\n      * Use for quick operations that complete within 60 seconds\n      * Commands run directly and wait for completion\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="default" blocking="true">\n        ls -l\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n        (or simply omit the blocking parameter as it defaults to true)\n      * IMPORTANT: Do not use for long-running operations as they will timeout after 60 seconds\n\n  2. Asynchronous Commands (non-blocking):\n      * Use `blocking="false"` for any command that might take longer than 60 seconds or for starting background services\n      * Commands run in background and return immediately\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="dev" blocking="false">\n        npm run dev\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n      * Common use cases:\n        - Development servers (Next.js, React, etc.)\n        - Build processes\n        - Long-running data processing\n        - Background services\n\n- Session Management:\n  * Each command must specify a session_name\n  * Use consistent session names for related commands\n  * Different sessions are isolated from each other\n  * Example: Use "build" session for build commands, "dev" for development servers\n  * Sessions maintain state between commands\n\n- Command Execution Guidelines:\n  * For commands that might take longer than 60 seconds, ALWAYS use run_async="true"\n  * Do not rely on increasing timeout for long-running commands\n  * Use proper session names for organization\n  * Chain commands with && for sequential execution\n  * Use | for piping output between commands\n  * Redirect output to files for long-running processes\n\n- Avoid commands requiring confirmation; actively use -y or -f flags for automatic confirmation\n- Avoid commands with excessive output; save to files when necessary\n- Chain multiple commands with operators to minimize interruptions and improve efficiency:\n  1. Use && for sequential execution: `command1 && command2 && command3`\n  2. Use || for fallback execution: `command1 || command2`\n  3. Use ; for unconditional execution: `command1; command2`\n  4. Use | for piping output: `command1 | command2`\n  5. Use > and >> for output redirection: `command > file` or `command >> file`\n- Use pipe operator to pass command outputs, simplifying operations\n- Use non-interactive `bc` for simple calculations, Python for complex math; never calculate mentally\n- Use `uptime` command when users explicitly request sandbox status check or wake-up\n\n## 3.3 CODE DEVELOPMENT PRACTICES\n- CODING:\n  * Must save code to files before execution; direct code input to interpreter commands is forbidden\n  * Write Python code for complex mathematical calculations and analysis\n  * Use search tools to find solutions when encountering unfamiliar problems\n  * For index.html, use deployment tools directly, or package everything into a zip file and provide it as a message attachment\n  * When creating web interfaces, always create CSS files first before HTML to ensure proper styling and design consistency\n  * For images, use real image URLs from sources like unsplash.com, pexels.com, pixabay.com, giphy.com, or wikimedia.org instead of creating placeholder images; use placeholder.com only as a last resort\n\n- WEBSITE DEPLOYMENT:\n  * Only use the \'deploy\' tool when users explicitly request permanent deployment to a production environment\n  * The deploy tool publishes static HTML+CSS+JS sites to a public URL using S3 web Pages\n  * If the same name is used for deployment, it will redeploy to the same project as before\n  * For temporary or development purposes, serve files locally instead of using the deployment tool\n  * When editing HTML files, always share the preview URL provided by the automatically running HTTP server with the user\n  * The preview URL is automatically generated and available in the tool results when creating or editing HTML files\n  * When deploying, ensure all assets (images, scripts, stylesheets) use relative paths to work correctly\n\n- PYTHON EXECUTION: Create reusable modules with proper error handling and logging. Use for precise text matching\n  2. Combine with CLI tools for powerful searches\n  3. Save complex patterns to files for reuse\n  4. Test patterns with small samples first\n  5. Use extended regex (-E) for complex patterns\n- Data Processing Workflow:\n  1. Use grep to locate relevant files\n  2. Use head/tail to preview content\n  3. Use awk for data extraction\n  4. WORKFLOW MANAGEMENT\n\n## 5.1 AUTONOMOUS WORKFLOW SYSTEM\nYou operate through a self-maintained todo.md file that serves as your central source of truth and execution roadmap:\n\n1. Upon receiving a task, immediately create a lean, focused todo.md with essential sections covering the task lifecycle\n2. Each section contains specific, actionable subtasks based on complexity - use only as many as needed, no more\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Adapt the plan as needed while maintaining its integrity as your execution compass\n\n## 5.2 TODO.MD FILE STRUCTURE AND USAGE\nThe todo.md file is your primary working document and action plan:\n\n1. Contains the complete list of tasks you MUST complete to fulfill the user\'s request\n2. Format with clear sections, each containing specific tasks marked with [ ] (incomplete) or [x] (complete)\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Before every action, consult your todo.md to determine which task to tackle next\n6. The todo.md serves as your instruction set - if a task is in todo.md, you are responsible for completing it\n7. Update the todo.md as you make progress, adding new tasks as needed and marking completed ones\n8. Never delete tasks from todo.md - instead mark them complete with [x] to maintain a record of your work\n9. Once ALL tasks in todo.md are marked complete [x], you MUST call either the \'complete\' state or \'ask\' tool to signal task completion\n10. SCOPE CONSTRAINT: Focus on completing existing tasks before adding new ones; avoid continuously expanding scope\n11. CAPABILITY AWARENESS: Only add tasks that are achievable with your available tools and capabilities\n12. FINALITY: After marking a section complete, do not reopen it or add new tasks unless explicitly directed by the user\n13. STOPPING CONDITION: If you\'ve made 3 consecutive updates to todo.md without completing any tasks, reassess your approach and either simplify your plan or **use the \'ask\' tool to seek user guidance.**\n14. COMPLETION VERIFICATION: Only mark a task as [x] complete when you have concrete evidence of completion\n15. SIMPLICITY: Keep your todo.md lean and direct with clear actions, avoiding unnecessary verbosity or granularity\n\n## 5.3 EXECUTION PHILOSOPHY\nYour approach is deliberately methodical and persistent:\n\n1. Operate in a continuous loop until explicitly stopped\n2. Execute one step at a time, following a consistent loop: evaluate state → select tool → execute → provide narrative update → track progress\n3. Every action is guided by your todo.md, consulting it before selecting any tool\n4. Thoroughly verify each completed step before moving forward\n5. **Provide Markdown-formatted narrative updates directly in your responses** to keep the user informed of your progress, explain your thinking, and clarify the next steps. Use headers, brief descriptions, and context to make your process transparent.\n6. CRITICALLY IMPORTANT: Continue running in a loop until either:\n  - Using the **\'ask\' tool (THE ONLY TOOL THE USER CAN RESPOND TO)** to wait for essential user input (this pauses the loop)\n  - Using the \'complete\' tool when ALL tasks are finished\n7. For casual conversation:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** to properly end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n8. For tasks:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** when you need essential user input to proceed (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - Provide **narrative updates** frequently in your responses to keep the user informed without requiring their input\n  - Use \'complete\' only when ALL tasks are finished\n9. MANDATORY COMPLETION:\n  - IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after ALL tasks in todo.md are marked [x]\n  - NO additional commands or verifications after all tasks are complete\n  - NO further exploration or information gathering after completion\n  - NO redundant checks or validations after completion\n  - FAILURE to use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after task completion is a critical error\n\n## 5.4 TASK MANAGEMENT CYCLE\n1. STATE EVALUATION: Examine Todo.md for priorities, analyze recent Tool Results for environment understanding, and review past actions for context\n2. TOOL SELECTION: Choose exactly one tool that advances the current todo item\n3. EXECUTION: Wait for tool execution and observe results\n4. **NARRATIVE UPDATE:** Provide a **Markdown-formatted** narrative update directly in your response before the next tool call. Include explanations of what you\'ve done, what you\'re about to do, and why. Use headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting to enhance readability.\n5. PROGRESS TRACKING: Update todo.md with completed items and new tasks\n6. METHODICAL ITERATION: Repeat until section completion\n7. SECTION TRANSITION: Document completion and move to next section\n8. COMPLETION: IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' when ALL tasks are finished\n\n# 6. CONTENT CREATION\n\n## 6.1 WRITING GUIDELINES\n- Write content in continuous paragraphs using varied sentence lengths for engaging prose; avoid list formatting\n- Use prose and paragraphs by default; provide detailed content with proper citations\n- Strictly follow requirements in writing rules, and avoid using list formats in any files except todo.md\n\n## 6.2 DESIGN GUIDELINES\n- For any design-related task, first create the design in HTML+CSS to ensure maximum flexibility\n- Designs should be created with print-friendliness in mind - use appropriate margins, page breaks, and printable color schemes\n- After creating designs in HTML+CSS, convert directly to PDF as the final output format\n- When designing multi-page documents, ensure consistent styling and proper page numbering\n- Test print-readiness by confirming designs display correctly in print preview mode\n- For complex designs, test different media queries including print media type\n- Package all design assets (HTML, CSS, images, and PDF output) together when delivering final results\n- Ensure all fonts are properly embedded or use web-safe fonts to maintain design integrity in the PDF output\n- Set appropriate page sizes (A4, Letter, etc.) in the CSS using @page rules for consistent PDF rendering\n\n## Image Guidelines\n- ALWAYS use the Image Tool for image generation or image editing tasks\n- Write a single self-contained image prompt before calling the Image Tool\n- Clearly describe the main subject and overall composition\n- Explicitly specify the intended visual style and aesthetic\n- Provide exact text content if text is required; Stworzę teraz przewodnik dla programistów (Developer Guide) oraz dodatkowe przykłady integracji:\n\n<function_calls>\n<create-file file_path="docs/DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md">\n# V-Sentinel Developer Guide\n\n## Table of Contents\n1. [Getting Started](#getting-started)\n2. [Architecture Overview](#architecture-overview)\n3. [Module Reference](#module-reference)\n4. [API Documentation](#api-documentation)\n5. [Integration Examples](#integration-examples)\n6. [Best Practices](#best-practices)\n7. [Troubleshooting](#troubleshooting)\n8. [Contributing](#contributing)\n\n---\n\n## Getting Started\n\n### Prerequisites\n\n- Rust 1.70+ (recommended: latest stable)\n- Cargo package manager\n- Git\n- Docker (optional, for containerized deployment)\n\n### Installation\n\n```bash\n# Clone the repository\ngit clone https://github.com/vantisCorp/V-Sentinel.git\ncd V-Sentinel\n\n# Build the project\ncargo build --release\n\n# Run tests\ncargo test --all\n\n# Generate documentation\ncargo doc --no-deps --open\n```\n\n### Quick Start Example\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel::{Sentinel, Config, ThreatType};\n\n#[tokio::main]\nasync fn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {\n    // Initialize V-Sentinel with default configuration\n    let config = Config::from_env()?;\n    let sentinel = Sentinel::new(config).await?;\n    \n    // Start monitoring\n    sentinel.start().await?;\n    \n    // Scan for threats\n    let threats = sentinel.scan().await?;\n    for threat in threats {\n        println!("Detected: {:?}", threat);\n    }\n    \n    // Enable quantum-resistant encryption\n    sentinel.enable_quantum_crypto().await?;\n    \n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Overview\n\n### System Layers\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                    Application Layer                         │\n│   Mobile │ Cloud │ IoT │ Gaming │ Metaverse                 │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                   AI & Analytics Layer                       │\n│   AI Engine │ Neural Networks │ Behavioral │ Autonomous     │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                      Security Layer                          │\n│   Biometrics │ Threat Intel │ SIEM │ Audit │ Monitoring     │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                   Cryptography Layer                         │\n│   Quantum-Resistant │ Privacy │ Blockchain                  │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                       Core Layer                             │\n│   Core Engine │ Config │ Error Handling │ Performance       │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### Module Dependencies\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    A[Core] --> B[Config]\n    A --> C[Error Handling]\n    A --> D[Performance]\n    \n    E[Quantum] --> A\n    F[Privacy] --> E\n    G[Blockchain] --> F\n    \n    H[AI] --> A\n    I[Neural] --> H\n    J[Behavioral] --> I\n    K[Autonomous] --> J\n    \n    L[Biometrics] --> A\n    M[Threat Intel] --> L\n    N[SIEM] --> M\n    \n    O[Mobile] --> K\n    P[Cloud] --> K\n    Q[IoT] --> K\n    R[Gaming] --> K\n    S[Metaverse] --> K\n```\n\n---\n\n## Module Reference\n\n### Quantum Cryptography Module\n\nThe Quantum module provides post-quantum cryptographic algorithms resistant to quantum computer attacks.\n\n#### Features\n- **Crystals-Kyber**: Key encapsulation mechanism (KEM)\n- **Crystals-Dilithium**: Digital signatures\n- **SPHINCS+:** Hash-based signatures\n- **Falcon**: Lattice-based signatures\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_quantum::{QuantumManager, QuantumConfig, KeyType};\n\n// Create quantum manager\nlet config = QuantumConfig {\n    default_algorithm: KeyType::Kyber1024,\n    enable_hybrid_mode: true,\n    key_rotation_days: 90,\n};\n\nlet manager = QuantumManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Generate quantum-resistant keypair\nlet keypair = manager.generate_keypair(KeyType::Kyber1024).await?;\n\n// Encrypt data\nlet ciphertext = manager.encrypt(data, &keypair.public_key).await?;\n\n// Decrypt data\nlet plaintext = manager.decrypt(&ciphertext, &keypair.private_key).await?;\n\n// Sign data\nlet signature = manager.sign(message, &keypair.private_key).await?;\n\n// Verify signature\nlet valid = manager.verify(message, &signature, &keypair.public_key).await?;\n```\n\n### Privacy Module\n\nThe Privacy module implements privacy-preserving technologies for data protection.\n\n#### Features\n- **Zero-Knowledge Proofs**: Bulletproofs, zk-SNARKs, zk-STARKs\n- **Differential Privacy**: Laplace and Gaussian mechanisms\n- **Homomorphic Encryption**: BFV, CKKS, Paillier\n- **Secure Multi-Party Computation**: SPDZ, GMW, Yao\'s\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_privacy::{PrivacyManager, PrivacyConfig, ZkProofType};\n\nlet config = PrivacyConfig::default();\nlet manager = PrivacyManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Generate zero-knowledge proof\nlet proof = manager.generate_zk_proof(\n    ZkProofType::Bulletproof,\n    &secret_data,\n    &public_inputs\n).await?;\n\n// Verify the proof\nlet valid = manager.verify_zk_proof(&proof).await?;\n\n// Apply differential privacy\nlet private_data = manager.apply_differential_privacy(\n    &raw_data,\n    epsilon: 1.0,\n    delta: 1e-5\n).await?;\n\n// Homomorphic encryption\nlet encrypted = manager.homomorphic_encrypt(&data).await?;\nlet result = manager.homomorphic_evaluate(&encrypted, operation).await?;\nlet decrypted = manager.homomorphic_decrypt(&result).await?;\n```\n\n### Neural Networks Module\n\nThe Neural module provides deep learning capabilities for threat detection.\n\n#### Features\n- **Deep Learning Models**: CNN, LSTM, Transformers\n- **Graph Neural Networks**: GCN, GAT, GraphSAGE\n- **Federated Learning**: FedAvg, FedProx\n- **Reinforcement Learning**: PPO, DQN, SAC\n- **Explainability**: SHAP, LIME\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_neural::{NeuralManager, NeuralConfig, ModelType};\n\nlet config = NeuralConfig {\n    default_model: ModelType::Transformer,\n    enable_federated_learning: true,\n    federated_rounds: 10,\n};\n\nlet manager = NeuralManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Train a model\nlet model = manager.train_model(\n    ModelType::LSTM,\n    training_data,\n    validation_data\n).await?;\n\n// Make predictions\nlet predictions = manager.predict(&model, &input_data).await?;\n\n// Federated learning\nlet fl_result = manager.federated_train(\n    &model,\n    client_datasets,\n    aggregation_strategy: AggregationStrategy::FedAvg\n).await?;\n\n// Explain predictions\nlet explanation = manager.explain_prediction(&model, &input, Method::SHAP).await?;\n```\n\n### Biometrics Module\n\nThe Biometrics module provides multi-modal biometric authentication.\n\n#### Features\n- **Fingerprint Recognition**: Minutiae extraction, matching\n- **Facial Recognition**: ArcFace, DeepFace features\n- **Voice Recognition**: MFCC, speaker verification\n- **Behavioral Biometrics**: Keystroke, mouse, gait analysis\n- **Multi-Modal Fusion**: Score-level, feature-level fusion\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_biometrics::{BiometricsManager, BiometricType, FusionMethod};\n\nlet manager = BiometricsManager::new(Default::default())?;\n\n// Register user biometric\nlet template = manager.enroll(\n    user_id,\n    BiometricType::Fingerprint,\n    &biometric_data\n).await?;\n\n// Authenticate with single modality\nlet result = manager.authenticate(\n    user_id,\n    BiometricType::Facial,\n    &face_data\n).await?;\n\n// Multi-modal authentication\nlet multimodal_result = manager.multimodal_authenticate(\n    user_id,\n    vec![\n        (BiometricType::Fingerprint, &fingerprint_data),\n        (BiometricType::Facial, &face_data),\n        (BiometricType::Voice, &voice_data),\n    ],\n    FusionMethod::WeightedScore\n).await?;\n\nprintln!("Authentication confidence: {:.2}%", multimodal_result.confidence * 100.0);\n```\n\n### Autonomous Agents Module\n\nThe Autonomous module provides self-managing security agents.\n\n#### Features\n- **Multiple Agent Types**: Detection, Response, Scanner, Analyst, Remediator\n- **Agent Orchestration**: Task assignment, coordination\n- **Continuous Learning**: Reinforcement learning updates\n- **Policy Engine**: Rule-based enforcement\n- **Automated Remediation**: Safe rollback mechanisms\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_autonomous::{AutonomousManager, AgentType, AgentConfig};\n\nlet config = AgentConfig {\n    max_agents: 100,\n    learning_rate: 0.001,\n    enable_auto_remediation: true,\n    safety_checks_enabled: true,\n};\n\nlet manager = AutonomousManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Deploy an agent\nlet agent = manager.deploy_agent(AgentType::ThreatResponse).await?;\n\n// Assign a task\nlet task = manager.assign_task(\n    agent.id,\n    "Respond to DDoS attack on API server"\n).await?;\n\n// Monitor agent status\nlet status = manager.get_agent_status(agent.id).await?;\n\n// Enable continuous learning\nmanager.enable_continuous_learning().await?;\n\n// Automated remediation with rollback\nlet result = manager.remediate_threat(threat_id).await?;\nif !result.success {\n    manager.rollback_remediation(result.remediation_id).await?;\n}\n```\n\n### Metaverse Security Module\n\nThe Metaverse module provides security for virtual and augmented reality environments.\n\n#### Features\n- **VR Security**: Motion sickness monitoring, session protection\n- **AR Security**: Location privacy, real-world overlay protection\n- **Virtual World Protection**: Property guard, economy protection\n- **Avatar Security**: Authentication, deepfake detection\n- **Spatial Security**: Virtual boundaries, proximity security\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_metaverse::{MetaverseManager, MetaverseConfig, VrSecurityLevel};\n\nlet config = MetaverseConfig::default();\nlet manager = MetaverseManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Start VR session\nlet session = manager.start_vr_session(\n    user_id,\n    avatar_id,\n    "decentraland".to_string(),\n    VrSecurityLevel::Enhanced\n).await?;\n\n// Protect virtual asset\nmanager.protect_asset(\n    asset_id,\n    VirtualAssetType::Nft,\n    owner_id\n).await?;\n\n// Validate asset transfer\nlet valid = manager.validate_asset_transfer(\n    asset_id,\n    from_user,\n    to_user,\n    amount\n).await?;\n\n// Detect metaverse threats\nlet threats = manager.detect_threats().await?;\n\n// End session\nmanager.end_vr_session(session).await?;\n```\n\n---\n\n## API Documentation\n\n### REST API Endpoints\n\nThe V-Sentinel API follows RESTful conventions:\n\n| Endpoint | Method | Description |\n|----------|--------|-------------|\n| `/api/v1/threats` | GET | List all threats |\n| `/api/v1/threats` | POST | Report a threat |\n| `/api/v1/threats/{id}` | GET | Get threat details |\n| `/api/v1/scan` | POST | Initiate security scan |\n| `/api/v1/quantum/keygen` | POST | Generate quantum keys |\n| `/api/v1/neural/predict` | POST | Make AI prediction |\n| `/api/v1/biometrics/auth` | POST | Biometric authentication |\n| `/api/v1/metaverse/session` | POST | Start metaverse session |\n\n### Authentication\n\n```bash\n# API Key authentication\ncurl -H "X-API-Key: your-api-key" https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/threats\n\n# JWT authentication\ncurl -H "Authorization: Bearer your-jwt-token" https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/scan\n```\n\n### Example API Calls\n\n```bash\n# List threats\ncurl -X GET https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/threats \\\n  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \\\n  -H "Content-Type: application/json"\n\n# Start scan\ncurl -X POST https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/scan \\\n  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \\\n  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \\\n  -d \'{\n    "target": "192.168.1.0/24",\n    "scan_type": "comprehensive",\n    "modules": ["quantum", "neural", "behavioral"]\n  }\'\n\n# Generate quantum keys\ncurl -X POST https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/quantum/keygen \\\n  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \\\n  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \\\n  -d \'{\n    "algorithm": "kyber1024",\n    "key_usage": "encryption"\n  }\'\n```\n\n---\n\n## Integration Examples\n\n### Integration with SIEM Platforms\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_siem::{SiemIntegration, SiemPlatform};\n\n// Connect to Splunk\nlet splunk = SiemIntegration::new(SiemPlatform::Splunk, splunk_config)?;\nsentinel.integrate_siem(splunk).await?;\n\n// Forward events to SIEM\nsentinel.forward_to_siem(event).await?;\n```\n\n### Integration with Cloud Providers\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_cloud::{CloudManager, CloudProvider};\n\n// AWS integration\nlet aws_config = CloudConfig {\n    provider: CloudProvider::AWS,\n    region: "us-east-1",\n    credentials: aws_credentials,\n};\n\nlet cloud_manager = CloudManager::new(aws_config)?;\ncloud_manager.deploy_sentinel().await?;\n```\n\n### Integration with Existing Applications\n\n```rust\n// As middleware in web applications\nuse sentinel::middleware::SecurityMiddleware;\n\nlet app = tide::new();\napp.with(SecurityMiddleware::new(sentinel_config));\napp.at("/api").get(handle_request);\napp.listen("0.0.0.0:8080").await?;\n```\n\n---\n\n## Best Practices\n\n### Security Best Practices\n\n1. **Always use quantum-resistant encryption** for sensitive data\n2. **Enable multi-modal biometrics** for high-security authentication\n3. **Deploy autonomous agents** for 24/7 threat monitoring\n4. **Use federated learning** to preserve data privacy\n5. **Implement zero-trust architecture** with continuous verification\n\n### Performance Best Practices\n\n1. **Use async operations** for all I/O-bound tasks\n2. **Enable caching** for frequently accessed data\n3. **Configure appropriate batch sizes** for ML operations\n4. **Use connection pooling** for database connections\n5. **Monitor resource usage** with the Performance module\n\n### Configuration Best Practices\n\n```yaml\n# Recommended production configuration\nsentinel:\n  environment: production\n  \n  quantum:\n    algorithm: kyber1024\n    key_rotation_days: 90\n    \n  neural:\n    model: transformer\n    batch_size: 64\n    federated_learning: true\n    \n  autonomous:\n    max_agents: 100\n    auto_remediation: true\n    safety_checks: true\n    \n  monitoring:\n    metrics_interval: 60s\n    log_level: info\n```\n\n---\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### Common Issues\n\n#### Quantum Key Generation Fails\n```\nError: Key generation timeout\n```\n**Solution**: Ensure sufficient entropy is available. On Linux:\n```bash\nsudo apt-get install haveged\n```\n\n#### Neural Model Training OOM\n```\nError: Out of memory during training\n```\n**Solution**: Reduce batch size or enable gradient checkpointing:\n```rust\nlet config = NeuralConfig {\n    batch_size: 32,  // Reduce from 64\n    gradient_checkpointing: true,\n    ..Default::default()\n};\n```\n\n#### Biometric Authentication Low Confidence\n```\nWarning: Authentication confidence below threshold\n```\n**Solution**: Enable multi-modal authentication or adjust threshold:\n```rust\nlet config = BiometricsConfig {\n    confidence_threshold: 0.85,  // Lower from 0.95\n    multimodal_fusion: true,\n    ..Default::default()\n};\n```\n\n---\n\n## Contributing\n\n### Development Setup\n\n```bash\n# Fork and clone\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/V-Sentinel.git\ncd V-Sentinel\n\n# Create feature branch\ngit checkout -b feature/your-feature\n\n# Install development dependencies\ncargo install cargo-audit cargo-tarpaulin\n\n# Run tests\ncargo test --all\n\n# Check coverage\ncargo tarpaulin --out Html\n\n# Security audit\ncargo audit\n```\n\n### Pull Request Process\n\n1. Fork the repository\n2. Create a feature branch\n3. Write tests for new functionality\n4. Ensure all tests pass\n5. Update documentation\n6. Submit pull request\n\n### Code Style\n\n```bash\n# Format code\ncargo fmt\n\n# Run linter\ncargo clippy -- -D warnings\n```\n\n---\n\n## License\n\nV-Sentinel is licensed under the MIT License. │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### Module Statistics\n\n| Module | Lines | Description |\n|--------|-------|-------------|\n| Biometrics | 1,248 | Multi-modal biometric authentication |\n| Neural | 970 | Deep learning and federated learning |\n| Autonomous | 894 | Self-managing security agents |\n| Metaverse | 871 | VR/AR security |\n| Privacy | 866 | Zero-knowledge proofs and differential privacy |\n| Blockchain | 824 | Threat reputation and smart contracts |\n| AI | 731 | AI-powered threat detection |\n| Performance | 711 | System optimization |\n| Config | 708 | Configuration management |\n| Quantum | 650 | Post-quantum cryptography |\n| Monitoring | 625 | Real-time monitoring |\n| Error Handling | 612 | Error recovery mechanisms |\n| Gaming | 607 | Anti-cheat and game security |\n| Behavioral | 535 | Behavioral analysis |\n| Cloud | 526 | Cloud security |\n| Mobile | 521 | Mobile application security |\n| SIEM | 476 | SIEM platform integration |\n| Threat Intel | 459 | Global threat intelligence |\n| IoT | 442 | IoT device security |\n| Core | 133 | Base system functionality |\n\n---\n\n## Module Reference\n\n### Quantum Cryptography Module\n\nThe Quantum module provides post-quantum cryptographic algorithms resistant to quantum computer attacks.\n\n#### Features\n- **Crystals-Kyber**: Key encapsulation mechanism (KEM)\n- **Crystals-Dilithium**: Digital signatures\n- **SPHINCS+:** Hash-based signatures\n- **Falcon**: Lattice-based signatures\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_quantum::{QuantumManager, QuantumConfig, KeyType};\n\n// Create quantum manager\nlet config = QuantumConfig {\n    default_algorithm: KeyType::Kyber1024,\n    enable_hybrid_mode: true,\n    key_rotation_days: 90,\n};\n\nlet manager = QuantumManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Generate quantum-resistant keypair\nlet keypair = manager.generate_keypair(KeyType::Kyber1024).await?;\n\n// Encrypt data\nlet ciphertext = manager.encrypt(data, &keypair.public_key).await?;\n\n// Decrypt data\nlet plaintext = manager.decrypt(&ciphertext, &keypair.private_key).await?;\n\n// Sign data\nlet signature = manager.sign(message, &keypair.private_key).await?;\n\n// Verify signature\nlet valid = manager.verify(message, &signature, &keypair.public_key).await?;\n```\n\n### Privacy Module\n\nThe Privacy module implements privacy-preserving technologies for data protection.\n\n#### Features\n- **Zero-Knowledge Proofs**: Bulletproofs, zk-SNARKs, zk-STARKs\n- **Differential Privacy**: Laplace and Gaussian mechanisms\n- **Homomorphic Encryption**: BFV, CKKS, Paillier\n- **Secure Multi-Party Computation**: SPDZ, GMW, Yao\'s\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_privacy::{PrivacyManager, PrivacyConfig, ZkProofType};\n\nlet config = PrivacyConfig::default();\nlet manager = PrivacyManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Generate zero-knowledge proof\nlet proof = manager.generate_zk_proof(\n    ZkProofType::Bulletproof,\n    &secret_data,\n    &public_inputs\n).await?;\n\n// Verify the proof\nlet valid = manager.verify_zk_proof(&proof).await?;\n\n// Apply differential privacy\nlet private_data = manager.apply_differential_privacy(\n    &raw_data,\n    epsilon: 1.0,\n    delta: 1e-5\n).await?;\n\n// Homomorphic encryption\nlet encrypted = manager.homomorphic_encrypt(&data).await?;\nlet result = manager.homomorphic_evaluate(&encrypted, operation).await?;\nlet decrypted = manager.homomorphic_decrypt(&result).await?;\n```\n\n### Neural Networks Module\n\nThe Neural module provides deep learning capabilities for threat detection.\n\n#### Features\n- **Deep Learning Models**: CNN, LSTM, Transformers\n- **Graph Neural Networks**: GCN, GAT, GraphSAGE\n- **Federated Learning**: FedAvg, FedProx\n- **Reinforcement Learning**: PPO, DQN, SAC\n- **Explainability**: SHAP, LIME\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_neural::{NeuralManager, NeuralConfig, ModelType};\n\nlet config = NeuralConfig {\n    default_model: ModelType::Transformer,\n    enable_federated_learning: true,\n    federated_rounds: 10,\n};\n\nlet manager = NeuralManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Train a model\nlet model = manager.train_model(\n    ModelType::LSTM,\n    training_data,\n    validation_data\n).await?;\n\n// Make predictions\nlet predictions = manager.predict(&model, &input_data).await?;\n\n// Federated learning\nlet fl_result = manager.federated_train(\n    &model,\n    client_datasets,\n    aggregation_strategy: AggregationStrategy::FedAvg\n).await?;\n\n// Explain predictions\nlet explanation = manager.explain_prediction(&model, &input, Method::SHAP).await?;\n```\n\n### Biometrics Module\n\nThe Biometrics module provides multi-modal biometric authentication.\n\n#### Features\n- **Fingerprint Recognition**: Minutiae extraction, matching\n- **Facial Recognition**: ArcFace, DeepFace features\n- **Voice Recognition**: MFCC, speaker verification\n- **Behavioral Biometrics**: Keystroke, mouse, gait analysis\n- **Multi-Modal Fusion**: Score-level, feature-level fusion\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_biometrics::{BiometricsManager, BiometricType, FusionMethod};\n\nlet manager = BiometricsManager::new(Default::default())?;\n\n// Register user biometric\nlet template = manager.enroll(\n    user_id,\n    BiometricType::Fingerprint,\n    &biometric_data\n).await?;\n\n// Authenticate with single modality\nlet result = manager.authenticate(\n    user_id,\n    BiometricType::Facial,\n    &face_data\n).await?;\n\n// Multi-modal authentication\nlet multimodal_result = manager.multimodal_authenticate(\n    user_id,\n    vec![\n        (BiometricType::Fingerprint, &fingerprint_data),\n        (BiometricType::Facial, &face_data),\n        (BiometricType::Voice, &voice_data),\n    ],\n    FusionMethod::WeightedScore\n).await?;\n\nprintln!("Authentication confidence: {:.2}%", multimodal_result.confidence * 100.0);\n```\n\n### Autonomous Agents Module\n\nThe Autonomous module provides self-managing security agents.\n\n#### Features\n- **Multiple Agent Types**: Detection, Response, Scanner, Analyst, Remediator\n- **Agent Orchestration**: Task assignment, coordination\n- **Continuous Learning**: Reinforcement learning updates\n- **Policy Engine**: Rule-based enforcement\n- **Automated Remediation**: Safe rollback mechanisms\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_autonomous::{AutonomousManager, AgentType, AgentConfig};\n\nlet config = AgentConfig {\n    max_agents: 100,\n    learning_rate: 0.001,\n    enable_auto_remediation: true,\n    safety_checks_enabled: true,\n};\n\nlet manager = AutonomousManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Deploy an agent\nlet agent = manager.deploy_agent(AgentType::ThreatResponse).await?;\n\n// Assign a task\nlet task = manager.assign_task(\n    agent.id,\n    "Respond to DDoS attack on API server"\n).await?;\n\n// Monitor agent status\nlet status = manager.get_agent_status(agent.id).await?;\n\n// Enable continuous learning\nmanager.enable_continuous_learning().await?;\n\n// Automated remediation with rollback\nlet result = manager.remediate_threat(threat_id).await?;\nif !result.success {\n    manager.rollback_remediation(result.remediation_id).await?;\n}\n```\n\n### Metaverse Security Module\n\nThe Metaverse module provides security for virtual and augmented reality environments.\n\n#### Features\n- **VR Security**: Motion sickness monitoring, session protection\n- **AR Security**: Location privacy, real-world overlay protection\n- **Virtual World Protection**: Property guard, economy protection\n- **Avatar Security**: Authentication, deepfake detection\n- **Spatial Security**: Virtual boundaries, proximity security\n\n#### Usage\n\n```rust\nuse sentinel_metaverse::{MetaverseManager, MetaverseConfig, VrSecurityLevel};\n\nlet config = MetaverseConfig::default();\nlet manager = MetaverseManager::new(config)?;\n\n// Start VR session\nlet session = manager.start_vr_session(\n    user_id,\n    avatar_id,\n    "decentraland".to_string(),\n    VrSecurityLevel::Enhanced\n).await?;\n\n// Protect virtual asset\nmanager.protect_asset(\n    asset_id,\n    VirtualAssetType::Nft,\n    owner_id\n).await?;\n\n// Validate asset transfer\nlet valid = manager.validate_asset_transfer(\n    asset_id,\n    from_user,\n    to_user,\n    amount\n).await?;\n\n// Detect metaverse threats\nlet threats = manager.detect_threats().await?;\n\n// End session\nmanager.end_vr_session(session).await?;\n```\n\n---\n\n## API Documentation\n\n### REST API Endpoints\n\nThe V-Sentinel API follows RESTful conventions:\n\n| Endpoint | Method | Description |\n|----------|--------|-------------|\n| `/api/v1/threats` | GET | List all threats |\n| `/api/v1/threats` | POST | Report a threat |\n| `/api/v1/threats/{id}` | GET | Get threat details |\n| `/api/v1/scan` | POST | Initiate security scan |\n| `/api/v1/quantum/keygen` | POST | Generate quantum keys |\n| `/api/v1/neural/predict` | POST | Make AI prediction |\n| `/api/v1/biometrics/auth` | POST | Biometric authentication |\n| `/api/v1/metaverse/session` | POST | Start metaverse session |\n\n### Authentication\n\n```bash\n# API Key authentication\ncurl -H "X-API-Key: your-api-key" https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/threats\n\n# JWT authentication\ncurl -H "Authorization: Bearer your-jwt-token" https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/scan\n```\n\n### Example API Calls\n\n```bash\n# List threats\ncurl -X GET https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/threats \\\n  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \\\n  -H "Content-Type: application/json"\n\n# Start scan\ncurl -X POST https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/scan \\\n  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \\\n  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \\\n  -d \'{\n    "target": "192.168.1.0/24",\n    "scan_type": "comprehensive",\n    "modules": ["quantum", "neural", "behavioral"]\n  }\'\n\n# Generate quantum keys\ncurl -X POST https://api.vsentinel.com/v1/quantum/keygen \\\n  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \\\n  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \\\n  -d \'{\n    "algorithm": "kyber1024",\n    "key_usage": "encryption"\n  }\'\n```\n\n---\n\n## Integration Examples\n\n### Integration with SIEM web applications\nuse sentinel::middleware::SecurityMiddleware;\n\nlet app = Practices\n\n1. **Always use quantum-resistant encryption** for sensitive data\n2. **Enable multi-modal biometrics** for high-security authentication\n3. **Deploy autonomous agents** for 24/7 threat monitoring\n4. **Use federated learning** to preserve data privacy\n5. **Implement zero-trust architecture** with continuous verification\n\n### Performance Best Practices\n\n1. **Use async operations** for all I/O-bound tasks\n2. **Enable caching** for frequently accessed data\n3. **Configure appropriate batch sizes** for ML operations\n4. **Use connection pooling** for database connections\n5. **Monitor resource usage** with the Performance module\n\n### Configuration Best Practices\n\n```yaml\n# Recommended production configuration\nsentinel:\n  environment: production\n  \n  quantum:\n    algorithm: kyber1024\n    key_rotation_days: 90\n    \n  neural:\n    model: transformer\n    batch_size: 64\n    federated_learning: true\n    \n  autonomous:\n    max_agents: 100\n    auto_remediation: true\n    safety_checks: true\n    \n  monitoring:\n    metrics_interval: 60s\n    log_level: info\n```\n\n---\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### Common Issues\n\n#### Quantum Key Generation Fails\n```\nError: Key generation timeout\n```\n**Solution**: Ensure sufficient entropy is available. On Linux:\n```bash\nsudo apt-get install haveged\n```\n\n#### Neural Model Training OOM\n```\nError: Out of memory during training\n```\n**Solution**: Reduce batch size or enable gradient checkpointing:\n```rust\nlet config = NeuralConfig {\n    batch_size: 32,  // Reduce from 64\n    gradient_checkpointing: true,\n    ..Default::default()\n};\n```\n\n#### Biometric Authentication Low Confidence\n```\nWarning: Authentication confidence below threshold\n```\n**Solution**: Enable multi-modal authentication or adjust threshold:\n```rust\nlet config = BiometricsConfig {\n    confidence_threshold: 0.85,  // Lower from 0.95\n    multimodal_fusion: true,\n    ..Default::default()\n};\n```\n\n---\n\n## Contributing\n\n### Development Setup\n\n```bash\n# Fork and clone\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/V-Sentinel.git\ncd V-Sentinel\n\n# Create feature branch\ngit checkout -b feature/your-feature\n\n# Install development dependencies\ncargo install cargo-audit cargo-tarpaulin\n\n# Run tests\ncargo test --all\n\n# Check coverage\ncargo tarpaulin --out Html\n\n# Security audit\ncargo audit\n```\n\n### Pull Request Process\n\n1. This document provides guidelines and instructions for contributing to the project.\n\n## Table of Contents\n- [Code of Conduct](#code-of-conduct)\n- [Getting Started](#getting-started)\n- [Development Workflow](#development-workflow)\n- [Coding Standards](#coding-standards)\n- [Testing](#testing)\n- [Documentation](#documentation)\n- [Pull Request Process](#pull-request-process)\n- [Reporting Issues](#reporting-issues)\n\n## Code of Conduct\n\nWe are committed to providing a welcoming and inclusive environment for all contributors. Please be respectful and constructive in all interactions.\n\n## Getting Started\n\n### Prerequisites\n\n- Rust 1.70+ (latest stable recommended)\n- Git\n- Docker (optional, for containerized testing)\n\n### Initial Setup\n\n```bash\n# Fork the repository\nfork and clone your fork\n\n# Add upstream remote\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/vantisCorp/V-Sentinel.git\n\n# Install development dependencies\ncargo install cargo-audit cargo-tarpaulin cargo-deny cargo-outdated\n\n# Run tests to verify setup\ncargo test --all\n```\n\n## Development Workflow\n\n1. **Create a branch** for your changes:\n   ```bash\n   git checkout -b feature/your-feature-name\n   ```\n\n2. **Make your changes** following the coding standards.\n\n3. **Test your changes**:\n   ```bash\n   # Run all tests\n   cargo test --all\n   \n   # Run integration tests\n   cargo test --test integration_tests\n   \n   # Check formatting\n   cargo fmt -- --check\n   \n   # Run linter\n   cargo clippy --all-targets --all-features -- -D warnings\n   ```\n\n4. **Commit your changes** with clear messages:\n   ```bash\n   git commit -m "feat: add quantum-resistant encryption support"\n   ```\n\n5. **Push to your fork**:\n   ```bash\n   git push origin feature/your-feature-name\n   ```\n\n6. **Create a Pull Request** to the main repository.\n\n## Coding Standards\n\n### Rust Conventions\n\nFollow the official [Rust Style Guide](https://rust-lang.github.io/api-guidelines/) and [Rust API Guidelines](https://rust-lang.github.io/api-guidelines/).\n\n### Code Formatting\n\nAll code must be formatted using `rustfmt`:\n```bash\ncargo fmt\n```\n\n### Linting\n\nAll code must pass `clippy` with no warnings:\n```bash\ncargo clippy --all-targets --all-features -- -D warnings\n```\n\n### Naming Conventions\n\n- **Modules**: `snake_case`\n- **Structs/Enums**: `PascalCase`\n- **Functions/Methods**: `snake_case`\n- **Constants**: `SCREAMING_SNAKE_CASE`\n- **Type Parameters**: `PascalCase` (e.g., `T`, `U`, `K`)\n\n### Documentation\n\nAll public items must have documentation comments:\n```rust\n/// Encrypts data using the specified algorithm.\n///\n/// # Arguments\n/// * `data` - The data to encrypt\n/// * `algorithm` - The encryption algorithm to use\n///\n/// # Returns\n/// Encrypted data as a vector of bytes\n///\n/// # Errors\n/// Returns an error if encryption fails\n///\n/// # Example\n/// ```\n/// let encrypted = encrypt(data, Algorithm::AES256)?;\n/// ```\npub async fn encrypt(data: &[u8], algorithm: Algorithm) -> Result<Vec<u8>, Error> {\n    // implementation\n}\n```\n\n### Error Handling\n\nUse the `Result` type for error handling:\n```rust\npub type Result<T> = std::result::Result<T, Error>;\n\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)]\npub enum Error {\n    #[error("Encryption failed: {0}")]\n    EncryptionError(String),\n    \n    #[error("Invalid key")]\n    InvalidKey,\n    \n    #[error("IO error: {0}")]\n    Io(#[from] std::io::Error),\n}\n```\n\n### Async/Await\n\nUse `async`/`await` for I/O operations and long-running tasks:\n```rust\npub async fn process_data(data: &[u8]) -> Result<Vec<u8>> {\n    // async implementation\n}\n```\n\n## Testing\n\n### Unit Tests\n\nWrite unit tests for all public functions:\n```rust\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn test_encryption() {\n        let data = b"test data";\n        let encrypted = encrypt(data, Algorithm::AES256).await.unwrap();\n        assert!(!encrypted.is_empty());\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Integration Tests\n\nAdd integration tests in the `tests/` directory:\n```rust\n// tests/integration_tests.rs\n\n#[tokio::test]\nasync fn test_module_integration() {\n    // integration test\n}\n```\n\n### Test Coverage\n\nMaintain test coverage above 80%:\n```bash\n# Run coverage\ncargo tarpaulin --out Html --output-dir coverage\n\n# View coverage report\nopen coverage/index.html\n```\n\n### Benchmarks\n\nAdd benchmarks for performance-critical code:\n```rust\n#[bench]\nfn bench_encryption(b: &mut test::Bencher) {\n    let data = vec![0u8; 1024];\n    b.iter(|| encrypt(&data, Algorithm::AES256));\n}\n```\n\n## Documentation\n\n### Inline Documentation\n\nDocument all public APIs with clear examples:\n```rust\n/// Example usage of the encryption module\n///\n/// ```\n/// use sentinel::crypto::encrypt;\n/// let encrypted = encrypt(b"data", Algorithm::AES256)?;\n/// # Ok::<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>>(())\n/// ```\n```\n\n### Module Documentation\n\nProvide overview documentation at the module level:\n```rust\n//! # Quantum Cryptography Module\n//!\n//! This module provides post-quantum cryptographic algorithms\n//! resistant to quantum computer attacks.\n//!\n//! ## Features\n//! - Crystals-Kyber key encapsulation\n//! - Crystals-Dilithium digital signatures\n//! - Hybrid encryption modes\n//!\n//! ## Usage\n//! ```\n//! use sentinel_quantum::QuantumManager;\n//! let manager = QuantumManager::new(config)?;\n//! let keypair = manager.generate_keypair(KeyType::Kyber1024).await?;\n//! ```\n```\n\n### README Updates\n\nUpdate the README when adding new features or changing APIs.\n\n## Pull Request Process\n\n### Before Creating a PR\n\n1. **Check for existing PRs**: Search for similar changes\n2. **Update documentation**: Ensure docs are up to date\n3. **Run all tests**: Ensure all tests pass\n4. **Check formatting**: Run `cargo fmt`\n5. **Run linter**: Run `cargo clippy`\n\n### PR Description Format\n\nUse the following format for PR descriptions:\n\n```markdown\n## Description\nBrief description of what this PR does and why.\n\n## Changes\n- Added feature X\n- Fixed bug Y\n- Updated documentation for Z\n\n## Testing\n- Unit tests: ✅\n- Integration tests: ✅\n- Manual testing: ✅\n\n## Checklist\n- [x] Code follows project style guidelines\n- [x] Tests added/updated\n- [x] Documentation updated\n- [x] All tests passing\n- [x] No clippy warnings\n```\n\n### PR Review Process\n\n1. **Automated checks**: CI/CD pipeline must pass\n2. **Code review**: At least one maintainer approval required\n3. **Testing**: Manual testing if needed\n4. **Merge**: After all approvals and checks pass\n\n## Reporting Issues\n\n### Bug Reports\n\nUse the bug report template:\n\n```markdown\n## Description\nClear description of the bug\n\n## Steps to Reproduce\n1. Step one\n2. Step two\n3. Step three\n\n## Expected Behavior\nWhat should happen\n\n## Actual Behavior\nWhat actually happens\n\n## Environment\n- OS: \n- Rust version: \n- V-Sentinel version: \n\n## Logs/Error Messages\n```\n\n### Feature Requests\n\nUse the feature request template:\n\n```markdown\n## Problem Statement\nWhat problem does this feature solve?\n\n## Proposed Solution\nHow should this feature work?\n\n## Alternatives\nWhat alternatives have you considered?\n\n## Additional Context\nAny other relevant information\n```\n\n### Security Issues\n\nFor security vulnerabilities, please email **security@vsentinel.com** instead of using public issues.\n\n## Recognition\n\nContributors are recognized in the project\'s CONTRIBUTORS.md file. All contributions are appreciated!\n\n## Questions?\n\n- Join our [Discord](https://discord.gg/vsentinel)\n- Open a [discussion](https://github.com/vantisCorp/V-Sentinel/discussions)\n- Email us at **contributions@vsentinel.com**\n\n## License\n\nBy contributing to V-Sentinel, you agree that your contributions will be licensed under the MIT License.\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}
